96 (Tue 7/20) 30ish miles\n\nWhenever we end up sleeping in a group of people, we get a reminder that everyone else starts way earlier than we do. Regardless, we packed up and hiked out. It's a long day of desert hiking, which is beautiful in how far you can see, but also is not the most visually dynamic. There's a reservoir that everyone on Guthook says you have to go to to cool off. We get there around noon, but somehow it also manages to be overcast the one day in the desert we're at a water source that hasn't been ruined by cows. Still we hang out regardless even if it isn't quite the oasis it would have been had the weather been hotter. I also finally see some of the wild horses of the basin! 75 (Tue 6/29): ??? miles\n\nSo after a rough night (no water, mildly heavy winds) I wake up and find that Nude Beach arrived later, that we passed Bison in the dark, and that we weren't too far from each other. No PDF, though. So I pack up and we start a steep, dangerous descent. There's no visible trail and it's all scree (small rocks that basically act as marbles when hiking). I'm very happy I didn't try to do this at night. I fall on my butt a few times, and after finally reaching the bottom and getting to water I find that both my water bottles had fallen out. Bison gave me one of his to use until we get to town. After regrouping with Nude Beach we have a meal break before starting a wild climb up and through the Argentine Ridge. This is the knifiest ridge ever, and as we get close to Gray's Peak (the highest point on trail) we are enveloped by clouds again. We get a message from PDF, who took a low route last evening and stopped just short of where we had planned to stop (but didn't make it to). He then got up early thinking we were ahead and was up and over Gray's Peak already. So we're feeling better about that, and we're feeling worse as we ascend the mountain because we hear thunder near the top. The worst place you can be when there may be lightning. We lose each other because of the clouds, but I run up to the top, snap a selfie (which I don't show now because it looks the same as my photo from yesterday), and start descending immediately. Luckily the other side is a well maintained trail and is easy to move quickly on. Once I clear the weather and feel safer, I start to run because I'm hungry and know at the end of this long dirt road is Bison's mom and aunt who will take us for food. We get picked up and find that his family made t-shirts from us! We go for dinner, grab Epson salts and breakfast foods, then back to the hotel.\n\nAlbums: Bacchanal 'N' Philadelphia by Mischief Brew. Approaching Thunder by We The Heathens. Chad Hates George self titled This week‚Äôs episode in @bigbendnps is no exception. Why do some among us behave so irresponsibly?\n‚Üü\nOne theory I‚Äôm willing to test states that our rash of recent infractions are simply due to the percentages. Since COVID forced so many indoors for so long, a higher number of people than before recreate outdoors upon emergence from lock-down. These large numbers also translate into a higher number (but equal %) of yo-yos spending time in campgrounds, national parks, and on hiking trails. More people, more dupewads. Thankfully, I actually noticed far fewer people on our local trails in 2021 than in 2020, so if this percentage play really does correlate with these increases in irresponsible behavior, then I‚Äôm satisfied that as this crazy world eventually returns to ‚Äúnormal,‚Äù the crowds and number of bozos will eventually diminish.\n‚Üü\nAnother theory I have is that ubiquitous cameras and closed-network sharing are to blame. While it can be easy to throw rocks at online social media as the root of modern evil, I think the problem is more elegant than that. The fact is, we simply don‚Äôt see that many idiots bragging online about their heinous acts of destruction. If and when the morons do take to social media for their public flaunting, such acts often get quickly shamed, rather than celebrated. Nevertheless, because every pocket now carries a camera, those troubled enough to vandalize also have the effortless ability to record their diabolical deeds; not for the world to see and celebrate,
